Spring and Autumn

Wu Yan's Notes 200

— Zhan Lu

Wu Yan criticizes people from the perspective of their state, called looking at someone's countenance; criticizes people from the perspective of their substance, called someone's raw material. Speaking of countenance, there is praise and derogation; speaking of raw material, there is only derogation and no praise.

Countenance has praise and derogation, for example; if there is a good countenance, there is also a bad countenance; all of which are blessed countenance, clean countenance, good-looking countenance, there is a countenance to do, are all nouns of praise. All of which are called beggar's countenance, dirty countenance, repulsive countenance, frivolous countenance, are all nouns of derogation.

Raw material has only derogation and no praise, for example; there is only bad raw material, no good raw material; all of which are robber's raw material, gangster's raw material, annoying raw material, beggar's raw material, lazy student's raw material, beggar's raw material, troublemaker's raw material, and even stupid raw material, dead raw material, beating raw material, killing raw material, are all nouns of derogation. It can be seen that inside the raw material, you can hardly find a noun of praise.

Other than countenance and raw material, there are also descriptions of people's mouths, faces, eyebrows, faces, most of which are nouns of derogation. For example; raised mouth, drooping face, dull old face, furrowed brow, bitter face.

There are also descriptions of people's styles and demeanors, called so-and-so, which are also nouns of derogation. For example; describing people who don't know how to move, called dead style, strange air; describing people who have calmed down, called yin style, strange air. Recent people write yin style, strange air, as yin and yang, strange air, which is really a mistake; changing style to yang, completely makes no sense. If yin style, strange air, can be written as yin and yang, strange air, then, dead style, strange air, can also be written as dead yang, strange air? Since dead yang, strange air, is known not to be a noun, then, yin and yang, strange air, is of course not a noun either, it is necessary to correct the mistake of taking style as yang.

Shaving 201

— Long Sao

Until recently; a friend gave me a Valet razor. Therefore, the black whiskers and stubble on my lips, which I never liked to decorate, had a tool for eradication. When I was bored, I borrowed its sharpness and used enough means to clear it up without leaving half a root.

Looking at my shiny face, some people would say that I am only about twenty years old. My wife, therefore, often pouts her small red lips, puts her arms around my neck, and is sincerely willing to kiss me, forming a pair of exquisite mouth bottles. The nectar flowing in the bottle will nourish the lonely flowers of life. At that time, I felt comfortable, and my soul grew red wings and flew. A kind of warm love flowed around my whole body, so I thanked the razor, praised the razor, and even understood "the great function of the knife in the world."

As long as there is a knife, everything that you don't want to exist can be removed. Saying it can kill people, suppress bandits, or resist Japan, shaving is just "a small matter."

But because I admired the knife and felt the annoyance of the beard at the same time, I often sharpened the knife to a silver-like shine. Looking in the mirror, I saw how I used my skills to scrape down the unresisting beards one by one, batch by batch. I smiled, and my wife hurried over to stroke my long, soft curly hair.

To retrieve my lost "pride of youth" from this embarrassment, I have no choice but to shave. At first, it was once a week, then once every four or five days. But now, it must be shaved once every two or three days. And the beard is getting thicker and stronger, not as docile as before. I'm afraid the blade will be broken one day? Later, I realized that because I didn't scrape the roots of the beard, it would be resurrected more quickly. There is no other way but to eradicate it fundamentally.

"But the beard is getting more and more after shaving!" My wife said.

So I began to doubt the insufficiency of "the military power of the knife." But seeing that my beard was like a hedgehog, and the shape was terrifying, I regretted that I had been misguided by the "authority of the knife" in the past. But what's the use of regretting it? Thinking of the poem "Wildfires can't burn them out, spring breeze blows them again," it further confirms that "if you want to destroy the long beard, you must cut off its roots." But my friend L, he is used to plucking his beard with silver tongs, but his forehead is still full of blue shadows. Saying this, the beard is something that is bound to grow in physiology, it has a kind of latent energy, and people of mature age have this inevitable annoying embellishment. To suppress it with "the military power of the knife," to eradicate it painfully, how can you guarantee that it will not resist and disappear!

Of course, there is more than one person in the world who shaves, but unfortunately they don't understand this philosophy at all. Therefore, wars are constantly happening everywhere.

Random Talk on Cartoons 202

— Composed by Can Yun, Illustrated by Lian Liang

，Drink this cup, skip a meal.

Bitterness and joy will never be balanced. Yet, the thirst for drink and the hunger for food are innate since birth, unchangeable. How many struggles aren't driven by hunger and thirst?

Humans are indeed perceptive creatures. In the sweltering heat, there are so many delightful, refreshing, and thirst-quenching delicacies. It's just that, like some people, if drinking a cup means forgoing a meal, wouldn't they humorously drink tap water instead!

Loquat Boats 203

— Lao Ren

"The trees are lush with jade leaves, the branches stacked with golden orbs." This is a classic verse praising loquats. In mid-summer of May, when the fruits are ripe, a special feature is added to the scenery of the Yuanyang Lake. Small boats, stern to stern, are filled with loquats, moving back and forth in the narrow waterways like butterflies flitting through flowers. The villagers harbor great hope, for their year's harvest hinges on these few days!

The origin of these small boats is ancient and untraceable. They are entirely native to Tangqi Town. Every year, as the loquats ripen, they begin a full-scale mobilization, transporting the fruits earned with their sweat and blood, basket by basket, boat by boat, towards Yuanyang Lake. It is said that Jiaxing is a land of gold, where good prices can be obtained. However, most people believe that the loquats from these boats are cheaper than those sold in the city markets, so they flock to them eagerly!

Tangqi is a small town under the jurisdiction of Hang County, about one hundred and several tens of li away from Jiaxing. The townspeople are simple and honest, and the villagers are diligent in farming. Every household grows loquats, creating the only natural orchard in China. The products are comparable to those of Dongting Mountain, with annual sales of about two to three million yuan. In addition to shipping to major ports such as Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Nanjing, Jiaxing is the second largest sales market. Every year, more than a hundred small boats gather inside and outside the city walls. The daily turnover is calculated in thousands of yuan, which is quite impressive. However, the people of Jiaxing have a greater fondness for loquats than anywhere else. "Every household eats loquats," which promotes brisk sales.

The construction of the loquat boats is similar to the yachts on West Lake, but on a smaller scale. In addition to being filled with loquats, a space is set aside for the boatmen to sleep and cook. It takes at least two days to travel from Tangqi to Jiaxing. Therefore, the villagers always go out fully loaded. After arriving at their destination, they work hard day and night. During the peak sales period, a boatload of loquats can be sold out in three or four days. Then, they exchange the money for rice and cloth and return home. This happens once a year, without interruption. Their lives are honest and sacred, worthy of admiration and respect!

Yesterday and today are vastly different. Human affairs are changing, and the national crisis is upon us. The impact has even spread to the sacred loquat boats. This year is very different from the past. Most of the temporary fruit boats from Tangqi Town have stopped moving forward. Even if there are any, they are few in number. It is said that the government, unable to collect taxes elsewhere, has suddenly set its sights on them, charging each boat two yuan for a donation fee, euphemistically called a license fee. Yesterday, I happened to chat with a boatman. He said that in the past, a boat full of loquats could be sold out in at most four or five days, but this year is completely different. Small boats come and go in the river, but no one cares about them, resulting in the spoilage of fresh fruit and great losses. Now is a time of rural economic collapse. The lives of farmers are difficult and arduous, reaching an extreme point. If farmers are further oppressed, the rural economy will never have a chance to recover. Alas! Harsh taxes are more ferocious than tigers," what more can I say.

Novel

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 204

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nine: Banter is not without reason; a dark plot leads to an unexpected outcome; the Western tutor quietly schemes.

Suddenly, Madam Jiang shouted out, "Old maiden, what's wrong with you?" She grabbed a fire poker and kept poking at the furnace. "I reckon you've poked it over a hundred times. If you keep poking, you'll break through the furnace." Only then did Guizhi wake up. Thinking to herself, "I must calm down and not show my unease," she smiled and said, "The briquettes are burning too hot and have turned into a lump. I can't break them apart without poking." She quickly added more briquettes and immediately slipped back into her room. Madam Jiang said, "That Miss Huang has been in the backyard for such a long time. I wonder if she'll have lunch with us. Go and see." Guizhi said, "I won't look, I won't bother." Madam Jiang said, "What are you saying? She treated you yesterday, and you won't bother today?" Guizhi said, "I'm not saying I won't entertain her, I'm saying I won't go to the backyard to find her." Madam Jiang said, "If you don't go, I will, or else people will really say we're too unreasonable." As Madam Jiang spoke, she was about to walk toward the backyard. Guizhi ran forward and grabbed her sleeve, saying, "Don't go either." Madam Jiang was surprised and looked at her, asking, "Then why?" Guizhi's face flushed slightly, and a faint smile emerged from the blush. Seeing this, Madam Jiang felt somewhat awkward and said, "Are you saying that they're having a heart-to-heart talk, and we shouldn't interrupt?" Guizhi pouted, "How would I know?" Seeing this, Madam Jiang understood and smiled along. This made Guizhi even more suspicious. Madam Jiang thought that Huang Manying would not be coming for lunch, so she said nothing more. It wasn't until that afternoon that Huang Manying came out smiling and called out from the window, "Granny Yang, I'm going into the city. Sorry to have troubled you." Hearing this, Madam Jiang had to come out to see her off. Seeing Madam Jiang come out, she quickly walked forward. When she reached the gate, she stopped and waited for Madam Jiang to approach. Then, she whispered with a smile, "Old lady, to be honest with you, I came out of the city this time to help you. From the looks of things now, it's generally good. I don't know what you think. Company Commander Guan will probably come to your house in a day or two. When he arrives, just tell him what's on your mind." (103)

Children's Paradise

Children's Entertainment 205

— Xia Tianwu

Children, entertainment is very important to you. What do you do when you get home from school every day? Many improper games are harmful and useless to you. Don't you find those old-fashioned games monotonous and boring? Here, I offer you some new games. If you follow them and put them into practice, you will find them interesting and beneficial to both your body and mind. Now, take a careful look.

One-Eyed Coin Tapping 206

Place a coin on the edge of the table, with half of it sticking out. Ask a person to stand and circle the table, tapping the coin off as they pass. This seems simple, doesn't it? But it's not as easy as it seems. First, they have to close one eye. Second, before tapping the coin, they have to turn around. This makes it difficult, doesn't it? Because closing one eye changes the sense of distance and depth, and turning around slightly shakes the nervous system, making it difficult to see the coin's position accurately. Using the little finger is also more difficult than using the middle or index finger. If there are many people playing, two tables can be put together. Each person runs slowly, two or three steps apart, back and forth. They must not intentionally stop while running. The person who knocks the coin off the most times wins.

Blind Man Eating 207

This is a very funny game. The purpose is to practice the use of hands and feet and to cultivate composure. When playing, divide into groups of two. Each person uses a handkerchief to cover their eyes. Each person holds a half bowl of tea (or cocoa, etc., as they please) and a teaspoon. The two people stand facing each other, about an arm's length apart. Appoint another person as a witness. After shouting one, two, three, the two people start feeding each other tea with the teaspoon, only allowed to feed it into the other's mouth. Spilling is considered invalid. Each group does the same. The first to finish feeding and spill the least wins. When playing this game, be careful not to rush when feeding. Rushing will make you frantically search for the other person's mouth, causing you to spill and feed it somewhere else. The witness has a great responsibility, which is not to laugh during feeding, otherwise it is easy to cause things like choking.

Little Post Office 208

This is a game of grabbing seats. The method is to prepare several chairs, one less than the number of players. Before playing, each person names a postal address (this can be freely imagined). Everyone who joins the game must remember the addresses. After one person shouts one, two, three, everyone rushes forward to grab a seat, but the attitude must not be barbaric. As a result, one person will not be able to grab a seat. This person becomes the postman. The postman has the duty to deliver the mail. How does he deliver the mail? He can randomly say two of the postal addresses just mentioned. The two people who hear their address stand up immediately and exchange seats. During this exchange, the postman can grab their seats. If he grabs a seat, the remaining person becomes the postman. If he doesn't grab a seat, the original postman remains the postman. The purpose of this game is to practice memory and alert movements.

Tabletop Soccer 209

This method is played by ten people, divided into two teams. Each team is assigned positions: one goalkeeper, two defenders, and forwards, standing at corresponding positions around the table. They lean their heads toward the tabletop and are not allowed to move. After the kickoff, everyone tries their best to blow the ball into the opponent's goal. The ball can be a paper ball or half of a broken ping pong ball. The goals are any objects placed on both sides. In this game, because the positions of both sides are not allowed to move, it is impossible to blow the ball into the opponent's goal with only one person's strength. Therefore, there will be some very clever passing. When playing, pay attention to attacking when the opponent is unprepared and defending against the opponent's attacks. So, it is often possible to score when the opponent's goalkeeper is taking a breath. Adults should not play with children, because their strength is not as good!

Free Talk

Art of the Secondary Clown 210

— Feng Zhiyu

In some opera troupes in eastern Zhejiang, there is a role called "Second Painted Face," or, translated more elegantly, "Secondary Clown." Unlike the little clown, he does not play the unrestrained playboy, nor the domineering servant of the prime minister's family. He plays the boxing instructor who protects the young master, or the flattering guest of the young master. In short, his status is higher than the little clown, but his character is worse.

The righteous servant is played by an old man, first with remonstrance, and finally with martyrdom; the evil servant is played by a little clown, who only knows how to do evil and ultimately perishes. But the skills of the secondary clown are different. He has a bit of an upper-class appearance, understands some music, chess, calligraphy, and painting, and can also play drinking games and solve riddles. But he relies on powerful connections and bullies the common people. When someone is oppressed, he sneers a few times to his heart's content. When someone is framed, he screams and shouts a few times. However, his attitude is not always like this. He usually turns his face around and points out the shortcomings of his young master to the audience under the stage, shaking his head and making a face, saying, "Look at this guy, he's going to be in trouble this time!"

This last trick is the hallmark of the secondary clown. Because he does not have the stupidity of the righteous servant, nor the simplicity of the evil servant, he is a member of the educated class. He knows that what he relies on is an iceberg and cannot last long. He will have to help others in the future, so when he is being fed and sharing the leftovers, he has to pretend that he is not with this noble young master. The plays written by the secondary clowns, of course, do not have this role. Why would he? The plays written by the little clowns, that is, the playboys, also do not have this role, because they only see one side and cannot imagine it. This "Second Painted Face" is a role that the common people have seen through this kind of person, extracted the essence, and created.

As long as there are powerful connections in the world, there will definitely be evil forces. If there are evil forces, there will definitely be secondary clowns, and there will be the art of the secondary clown. We only need to pick up a publication and read it for a week, and we will find that it sometimes hates spring, sometimes praises war, sometimes translates Bernard Shaw's speeches, and sometimes talks about marriage problems; but sometimes it must express dissatisfaction with national affairs with慷慨激昂. This is using the last trick.

This last trick is also to cover up that he is not helping. However, the common people understand and have already made his type appear on the stage.

"Three-Story Building," "Antiques," and Others 211

— Shen Qiyu

In the past two days, there have been articles by Mr. Da Wu and Hu Qiuyuan in Free Talk about "Three-Story Building" and "Antiques." It so happens that I have also translated this book, so a sense of fear of falling into the same mistakes made me check my translation against the original text. Now that the matter of "Three-Story Building" has been resolved, I only want to talk about "Antiques" and others. I checked and found that the original text here is the word "Bibelo," which, in addition to meaning small ornaments, has the meaning of "MenusofbjecTSbepeudeValeut" (trivial things of little value). Translating it as "an antique" seems inappropriate. However, this overstepping is not on Mr. Hu's part but is actually due to the Japanese translator. Therefore, I also feel the real difficulty of "retranslation," although I also occasionally do retranslations of Russian books.

At the same time, in addition to "antiques" and other things, and translating "captain" as "capitalist" (see his discussion of Robinson Crusoe) due to carelessness, there are also many omissions and not small errors in the Japanese translation of Ikowitz's book. For example, in the section on Futurism, "VictoredeSamothracre" is translated as "the victory of Shamotras," which is really incomprehensible. The reason is: "Victoire" is the Greek goddess, the daughter of Pallas and Styx, and "VictoirediSamothrace" is a statue of Victoire discovered on the island of Samothrace in 1863. Although Victoire has the meaning of victory, that is only the same as Milkyway having the meaning of "milk road."

Retranslating is not good, but that does not mean that all translations done according to the original text are good. Even my translation of Ikowitz is something to be ashamed of. Also, recently, when reading Mr. Wu Simao's translation of Macha's "History of Western Art" (which is said to be translated directly from Russian), many places are incomprehensible to me no matter how I read them. It was only after comparing them with the Japanese translation that I understood what was going on. And there are also many errors in the annotations of the names in it, such as annotating Chardin as Sargent and annotating Greuze as GroS (see page six of the Kaiming edition), etc.

Although errors are inevitable for people, both retranslating and translating according to the original text are worthy of our efforts as translators.

Sleeping Pill 212

— Another Realm

Mr. Lang Sun discussed in Free Talk how modern youth are bewildered by the changes in society and history, which led Mr. Cao Juren to write an article entitled "My Bewilderment." Mr. Cao used Li Po's great dream as an example. Li Po slept for twenty years and woke up. Although the world was different and he had become a marginalized person, his despotic and ferocious wife had died. And Mr. Cao, "took a sleeping pill during the May Fourth Movement and spent ten years in a half-dreaming state, and now he suddenly woke up." Opening his eyes, he saw that, like Li Po, the world was different and he had become a very marginalized person, but his despotic and ferocious, heart-stopping "wife" had not died. Therefore, Mr. Cao wanted to take another sleeping pill and sleep for another ten years.

Very good, sleeping pills do exist, but I hope Mr. Cao will swallow it a little slower, wait for me. I am very eager to swallow a sleeping pill!

Probably there are more than just Mr. Cao and I who want to swallow sleeping pills!

There is nothing difficult about swallowing sleeping pills. We can very well sleep for ten or twenty years, "to hell with it." However, if the despotic and ferocious "wife" is still not dead when we wake up in ten or twenty years, does Mr. Cao plan to swallow it again? If Mr. Cao can be sure that the "wife" will definitely die by then, then Mr. Cao, let's do it.

Furthermore, I still have a little concern. We cannot be without a "wife," and we advocate free love. Even if that ferocious and despotic "wife" dies during our sleep, when we wake up, a new "wife" will have already been arranged for us. What then? Should we accept it or not?

I am afraid that Mr. Cao will feel bewildered again at that time, and will once again eagerly oppose the new "wife"!

So the problem is not swallowing sleeping pills, but finding a way to immediately leave the current despotic and ferocious wife and seek a happy companion.

A Ning 213

— Wang Wanrong

Such a thin girl! I muttered to myself, watching the swaying back of A Ning, the new maid the Li family across the street had hired.

For a month, I haven't seen her wearing shoes. How strange! Why is there a section of her left toe missing? Whenever she comes back with water, we always worry about her, fearing that she will accidentally fall and get scalded by boiling water. Look, the way she walks, twisting and swaying, is so worrying!

"Sister Ning, be careful! Why don't you wear a pair of socks? At least you should wear a pair of shoes! It's terrible to get scalded by boiling water."

"I'm used to it," she said with a charming smile.

"Why is there a section of your left toe missing?" I asked, looking at her foot in surprise.

"Miss Ying, I'll tell you next time when I have time! Look at all these scars on my body!" A Ning's melancholy gaze was fixed on her left foot, sighing deeply.

She’s always so busy going out to dump garbage, fetching water, taking their young master to school, and washing clothes by the river, that she never has time to tell me why she lost a section of her toe. Gradually, she grew thinner, and new bloodstains were often seen added to the old scars on her face. When asked, she just blushed and remained silent, turning into a petrified girl.

According to Xu Ma, her master's maid, A Ning lost her parents long ago. When she was eight years old, she was taken to her husband's family as a child bride. Every day, she had to cook, wash clothes, weave cloth, and work in the fields, but her in-laws still didn't like her. One night, she quietly sneaked out, but was discovered by her husband halfway, who chased her back, locked her up for a few days, and then sold her to the Li family.

"Why is there a section of her left toe missing?" Xu Ma was just as bewildered as I was.

One day, two days, three or four days passed without seeing A Ning's swaying waist.

"Xu Ma, what's wrong? What's wrong with your A Ning?"

"She's sick, Miss Ying."

"What's wrong with her?"

Xu Ma walked away as if she hadn't heard.

Ten days, twenty days, a month later, there was still no sign of A Ning.

"Xu Ma, what's wrong? Isn't your A Ning's illness getting better yet?" Xu Ma was silent. She looked around, walked closer to me, and said in a low voice, "She's dead. She's been buried for more than twenty days!"

"Ah!" I was stunned. "What did she die of?"

"Hey, Miss Ying, the weather is really nice today!" Xu Ma suddenly raised her voice, followed by a string of dry laughs.

I looked blankly at her face, which couldn't hide her panic. I found that Madam Li across the street was shooting two bright gazes at us from the window. "Xu Ma," she shouted sharply.

The next day, on the top floor, I saw Xu Ma carrying a small bundle and walking away in the morning light.

"Xu Ma," I wanted to shout, but I caught a glimpse of Madam Li across the street staring at me from the window.

"Ha, Miss Ying, how diligent! You're up so early?" she greeted me unnaturally.

Gradually, I understood everything.

Red Carrot Whiskers 214

— Written by Jule Renaro, Translated by Lin Qu

The Fishhook (Continued)

Lepic wanted to remove the hook.

"Ah, no! Don't do that!" Lepic's wife shrieked.

Indeed, the fishhook had completely penetrated her finger, one side showing the sharp point, the other the eye.

Lepic squinted at it.

"Damn," he said, "this has to be broken to get it out!"

How could the fishhook be broken! Lepic only needed to use a little force, and before he even grasped her firmly, she jumped up and screamed. Was he digging out her heart and taking her life? And the fishhook was made of extremely sharp steel.

"Then, the flesh has to be cut open," Lepic said.

He put his monocle on his eye, took out a small knife, and began to cut into her finger, but the blade was too dull to cut through. He pressed the knife onto the flesh and cut hard, causing some blood to flow.

"Ah! Ah!" Lepic's wife cried, making everyone tremble.

"Hurry, Papa!" said the girl, Elestine.

"Just bear with it!" said the older brother, Felix, to his mother.

Lepic lost his patience. The knife cut into the flesh, sawing wildly. Lepic's wife, after softly muttering "Executioner! Executioner!" fortunately fainted.

Lepic seized the opportunity to continue. His face was snow-white, and he cut like a madman, searching in the flesh, and the finger was fine!

While everyone was helping Lepic's wife remove the fishhook, Red Carrot Whiskers did not contribute any effort. When he heard his mother's first scream, he ran away. He sat on the stairs, holding his head in his hands, trying to figure out the cause of this accident. Undoubtedly, it must have been when he swung the fishing rod far away that the hook remained on his back.

"I now know why I couldn't catch any fish later!" he said. He listened to his mother sighing, initially without feeling any sadness. Wasn't it going to be his turn soon to scream like her, and to scream as much as possible, until he was exhausted and hoarse, so that she would realize that she had gotten enough revenge and spare him?

Some neighbors who had run over hearing the screams asked him:

"What exactly happened, Red Carrot Whiskers?"

He didn't answer; he covered his ears, and his auburn head disappeared. The neighbors lined up on the stairs, waiting to hear the news.

Lepic's wife finally came out. She was as pale as a woman who had just given birth. She seemed somewhat proud, as if she had overcome a great danger, and held her carefully bandaged finger in front of her. She had conquered the lingering pain. She smiled at the neighbors who had come to see her, said a few words to reassure them, and then gently said to Red Carrot Whiskers:

"You hurt me, my good boy! I don't blame you; it's not your fault."

She had never spoken to Red Carrot Whiskers in such a tone. He was surprised and raised his head. He saw that his mother's finger was wrapped in cloth and thread, clean, thick, and square, just like a poor child's toy. His dry eyes suddenly filled with tears.

Lepic's wife bent down. She put her elbows forward as usual. But very generously, in front of everyone, she embraced and kissed him. He was baffled. He cried uncontrollably.

"Since people have already told you that this is over, I forgive you, why are you still crying! Did you think it was really that terrible?"

Red Carrot Whiskers sobbed even more intensely.

"Isn't this stupid? People will definitely say someone is strangling him," Lepic's wife said to the neighbors who were moved by her kindness.

She handed them the fishhook, letting them examine it curiously. One of them asserted that it was a size eight hook. Slowly, she became eloquent again, and with her silver tongue, she recounted the tragedy to them. (To be continued)

Securities and Public Bonds 交 Clearing Hover 220

Only Whole Land Rises by Three or Four 角

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange experienced even more hovering in the market, leading to even clearer transactions. It was because although the bulls wanted to emerge, they were unwilling to reduce prices for sale. Although the bears wanted to cover, they were unwilling to raise prices. The two sides held each other back, resulting in a situation with no rise or fall. Looking at the overall trend, the bulls were relatively weaker. The bears took advantage of the bulls' slow emergence to cover their positions, and the two sides insisted on a difference of five points in the market price for a long time, making the market even more sluggish. The coming change was brewing in this situation. If there were no special changes in the environment, the market price would not undergo drastic changes for a while. Yesterday's prices had almost no rise or fall to speak of. Generally, bulls in numbers 11 and 50 emerged slightly, and bears in numbers 14, 35, and 59 covered slightly, but none of them were in a hurry, maintaining a state of approaching and separating. Each of the two morning and afternoon sessions had both rises and falls, and each only fluctuated by one or two jiao. Therefore, the result was that only whole land rose by three or four jiao, and other types rose by one or two jiao. Two types even fell by one jiao. The chaos and stagnation of the situation meant that changes were still brewing. The total transaction volume was 7,300,075 yuan, including 7,500 yuan in spot goods. Futures were dominated by the salt tax, accounting for 2,865,000 yuan, demobilization accounted for 1,170,000 yuan, the 19th Customs Good accounted for 720,000 yuan, the 20th Roll 20th Customs Good accounted for 1,210,000 yuan, and the 96th still had 540,000 yuan. Yarn and Flower Market Still Has Not Escaped a Weak State 222

The yarn market is still weak, and the situation is softening. Although American cotton has risen, it has failed to excite the people. This is because the current sales of yarn are too thin, and the amount of bottom goods is increasing daily. Therefore, the sellers have a strong mental attitude. However, factories are increasingly suffering from the high cost of raw materials, and some are proposing to reduce labor.

丨Two Yuan, Three Jiao, Three Fen丨

Amateur Musings

What If Lost Territories Are Recovered? 238

— Pu

Recently, Mr. Hollington K. Tong, a well-known figure in the American press, came to China to investigate the current situation in China and the state of the press. Leaders from all walks of life in Shanghai and the Daily Newspaper Association have held public banquets to welcome him sincerely. A reporter recently heard from a friend who had spoken with Mr. Tong (hereinafter referred to as Tong) that Tong is the director of major American newspapers and the Associated Press. He is very familiar with the situation in China. Once, at a banquet, Tong had a candid conversation with a certain gentleman about the past and future situation in the three northeastern provinces. Tong raised a profound question that made us feel painful and resentful. That is: "...If Japan suddenly implements a truly friendly policy with China and completely returns the three northeastern provinces and Rehe to China, let us speculate, whom will China send to accept and manage these four provinces of land?" We should know that the background of Tong's question is that he knows what the three northeastern provinces were like under the rule of Zhang Xueliang and what Rehe was like under the rule of Tang Yulin. Some people may want to retort that if Tong really had such an intention, then given the current state of political disorder in all provinces of the country, wouldn't it be necessary to ask foreigners to govern them? But at the same time, we can also say that China's current political chaos is largely caused by the imperialism and capitalism of the great powers. In this semi-colonial situation, there have arisen the political fragmentation, economic bankruptcy of rural areas, and the immaturity of industrial production. Therefore, if we want to create a new life for the nation and build a new country with political order, we must first break this semi-colonial environment and eliminate all international forces that oppress China politically and economically.

If we criticize the above two different Chinese and foreign observations of the Chinese problem with a purely objective and unemotional attitude, we feel that each has its own merits. Because the latter's argument starts from the overall political and economic situation of China, and the lesson given to us by Mr. Hollington K. Tong's question is how determined the national government leaders have been to resist Japan since the September 18th Incident and the loss of Rehe this year, and where are the facts of improving internal affairs. We don't have to resent the mockery of foreigners. We should pay attention to the various opportunistic mentalities shown by the government and the people since the national crisis. In the past, when Tianjin and Beiping were in danger and the troops were approaching the city, the government showed various signs of being flustered and unprepared beforehand, and indecisive at the time. If the government and the people of today are determined to break the current semi-colonial status of the country and eliminate all international forces that oppress China politically and economically, then, let us ask, from what can we see the facts of the government's preparation for this? And from what can we see the spirit of the people's determination?

Without preparation, without determination, the future of the national crisis has no end!

Beset on All Sides by Life's Many Aspects 239

— Wei Yiguang

(Seamen) Most Chinese seamen come from Shandong, Tianjin, Shanghai, Ningbo, Fuzhou, Guangzhou, Qiongya, Shantou, and other places. According to the work on ships, they can be divided into four types: stokers, sailors, stern, and mess hall. Because of language barriers, their regional concepts are very deep, which prevents them from forming close relationships with each other. At the same time, seamen who are sailors cannot be stokers, and those who are stokers cannot be stern or mess hall workers. The "She Ma Sha" (labor contractors) take advantage of this opportunity to divide and alienate the feelings of seamen from various places, so that the seamen cannot unite, and they have to submit obediently, allowing them to be exploited and oppressed.

The foremen on the ship are the figures who exploit the seamen together with the "She Ma Sha." Because every shipping company has a "She Ma Sha," the general bosses must use money to lobby the "She Ma Sha" in order to obtain the foreman's job. The "She Ma Sha" use various methods to make a group of foremen compete with each other. Whoever spends more tea money gets the job. The amount of money used is based on the size of the ship and the amount of profit. After the foreman gets a job on the ship, he goes to find a group of seamen to work. Everything is of course controlled by him, because they implement a contracting system. He finds seamen whose labor costs are low and calls them to work. For example, if the monthly salary for each person is 30 yuan, then the foreman will first say to them: "There is no salary for the first month, or only a few yuan are given. Are you willing to do it or not? And now there are so-and-so and others who are willing to work for three or two months without taking a salary!" Sometimes, when there is a business of smuggling goods, it is mostly handed over to the seamen to do, to take the fall. Once an arrest occurs, the responsibility of course falls on the seamen, and the seamen have to do this kind of knowingly illegal thing because they are forced by life.

These foremen, compradors, and senior staff often have opium lamps, fantan, pai gow, mahjong, poker, playing cards, etc. on the ship. On the one hand, they are of course set up for passengers, but on the other hand, they are to lure the seamen into the trap, so that they can extract a commission from them and enjoy the benefits. Opium lamps are their exclusive sales. They lure seamen to smoke in order to absorb their hard-earned money, so that their money is exhausted as soon as they get it and they are forced to borrow money from them. The interest rate on this loan is as high as one jiao to two jiao per yuan per month.

The working hours of seamen are at least 10 hours or more per day. Originally, for the hard work done by stokers and sailors, a maximum of five hours a day is enough. However, capitalists and compradors will not think about this. They just want to make money. Moreover, seamen are often scolded by the compradors, chief mate, second mate, chief engineer, second engineer, and foremen. No matter how they lose their temper, the seamen have to hold back their tears and force a smile!

As for the seamen's clothing, food, and housing on the ship, it is even more unspeakable. They live in houses that are only one zhang wide, with seven or eight or even more than ten people in each room, and they are in the hottest and most unclean places near the toilets and the stokehold. The clothing, shoes, and hats they wear should have been borne by the company, but because the foremen and "She Ma Sha" want to win the favor of the capitalists, they transfer all the seamen's clothing and soap to the seamen to take care of themselves. At the same time, the seamen's food is also contracted by the foremen. In name, the monthly food allowance is usually 10 to 12 yuan, but what they eat is the same as what dogs and pigs eat.

Finally, I want to talk about the health aspect on the ship. Originally, health should be emphasized on the ship, but all the doctors on the ship are hired entirely for the chief engineer, second engineer, chief mate, second mate, shipowner, and a few senior staff and senior passengers. If the seamen have a disease, they still have to work without rest. If they have a contagious disease that is dangerous, of course they cannot get up to work. Therefore, some conscientious foremen secretly take some medicine to help; if they tell the doctor, then this dog's life will be sent to the sea immediately. Because the doctors on the ship are most afraid of infectious diseases, if they know that a worker has an infectious disease, they will immediately use electricity or poison to kill him and throw him into the sea to avoid infecting the rest of the people on the ship. This is the sanitation on the ship!

An Interview with a Celebrity in the Business and Industrial World

An Interview with Mr. Zhu Zhiyao 240

— Wu Xingeng

(Comprador and Great Industrialist) Mr. Zhu Zhiyao, the grandnephew of the ninety-four-year-old Ma Xiangbo, once served as a ship comprador for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, manager of the Jiangnan Shipyard, and comprador for the Banque de l'Indochine. He founded the Qiuxin Factory, Lide Oil Factory, Tongchang Yarn Factory, Datong Renji and China United Navigation Companies, and is a great industrialist in Shanghai. Yesterday, I drove to visit him and was warmly welcomed. I am recording his conversation below:

(1) China Merchants Steam Navigation Company: I was introduced by a relative to become a ship comprador for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. When the ship reached the middle of the ocean, the wind and waves were strong, and the ship was rocking violently. I vomited and was in great pain. At that time, I realized that the life on the ship was hard. I thought that I was a pampered child from a wealthy family, enjoying comfortable food and clothing. Wouldn't it be asking for trouble to come here? Then I suddenly realized that people should strive to survive in the world. With this self-encouragement, I became a comprador for eighteen years. (2) Banque de l'Indochine: When I was a comprador for the Banque de l'Indochine, my nephew Yunwang came to learn to be a comprador, but he was idle. So I said to him, "If you want what you want, you might as well climb a tree to catch a fish." He was scolded by me and never came again. Later, he also entered the customs service. He likes to study physics and chemistry and has many instruments. One day, he invited me and the customs officer to his house for lunch. During the meal, he experimented with yin and yang electricity and generated lightning. The customs officer saw it and was amazed. So he was promoted to chemical inspector and has been doing it until now. (3) Qiuxin Factory: More than 30 years ago, I traveled overseas with my uncle, Xiangbo. Seeing the development of industry in Europe and the United States, I decided to revitalize China's industry. So I opened the Qiuxin Factory. I was willing to make all the machines that foreign countries had. Like the sock knitting machine, which was imported from foreign countries and sold for more than 200 taels each, I sold my own made ones for only 25 yuan each, and I sold as many as two or three thousand!

(4) Jiangnan Shipyard: Later, I was invited by a friend to serve as the manager of the Jiangnan Shipyard. I received several thousand dollars in wages in the first month, which surprised me, but at the same time, it also emboldened me. So at that time, I expanded the Qiuxin Factory, and I also got a guarantee from President Yuan, with remarkable credit and booming business.

(5) Lide Oil Factory: Using soybeans to squeeze oil, the beans are covered with cake cloth, and the squeezed liquid is soybean oil. Speaking of cake cloth, the material is very strong. Imported from foreign countries, each sheet sells for four or five taels. I thought it was too expensive and wanted to make it myself, so I telegraphed abroad to buy a machine for making cake cloth. The reply said that the machine had to be sold for tens of thousands of taels. Because the price was too expensive, I replaced it with a carpet. But, alas, the oil had not yet been squeezed out, but the carpet was already broken. Later, I thought of a method, hired three workers, took hemp skin and composed hemp thread, asked them to weave hemp cloth like weaving horse belly bands, and used it as cake cloth, no different from foreign goods. Alas, I didn't expect that a machine worth tens of thousands of taels could actually be replaced by manual labor. Do you think it's strange or not! (6) Datong and China United Navigation Companies: Datong Renji Shipping Company has four ships, specializing in the Tongyang route. China United Navigation Company was founded only four or five years ago. Now it has three ships, specializing in the Haizhou route. When these two companies were first founded, each had only 200,000 yuan in funds. Due to the development of the business, they now each have several million yuan in capital.

Current Affairs Research

Ten Million U.S. Dollars to Relieve the Wheat Famine 242

— Li

Because China is experiencing a wheat famine, Song Ziwen recently signed an agreement with the U.S. Treasury and the U.S. Rehabilitation Finance Corporation in the United States to borrow 50 million U.S. dollars (equivalent to more than 200 million Chinese currency). Four-fifths of this money is for buying cotton, and of course it is also because cotton is experiencing a famine. The rest is for buying wheat. It is said that this is beneficial to both parties; the surplus of the U.S. market can be sold, and Chinese people can be encouraged to use U.S. cotton and wheat. At the same time, the Chinese economy can also be reactivated, which is beneficial to the restoration of the world economy.

Let's just look at the benefits to both sides from the wheat aspect!

This transaction is of course very beneficial to U.S. imperialism, because it can dump its own country's overproduced wheat into China and also get a 5% interest rate!

What about semi-colonial China? Due to imperialist economic aggression, on the one hand, it accelerates the commercialization of agricultural production in China, so that the daily necessities needed in rural areas must rely more and more on markets full of imported goods. On the other hand, it destroys the family handicrafts in rural areas, separating it from agriculture and gradually becoming an independent production sector. The former increases the expenditures of farmers, while the latter reduces their income. Therefore, farmers are easily threatened by hunger. Exorbitant taxes, warlords, corrupt officials, and feudal landlords exploit the farmers, and the wars of Chinese warlords, with the conflicts between various imperialists as their background, are the inevitable result of conflicts with productive forces. Therefore, even though this year is a year of bumper harvests, the result is a bumper harvest turned into a disaster, and low grain prices hurt farmers. Because grain prices are low, even if farmers sell all the grain they harvest, the income is not enough to compensate for the debts, all the exorbitant taxes, and land rents. If American wheat is used for "relief," it will naturally cause the price of wheat produced in China to fall even further, and the result is that it will further accelerate the process of rural economic bankruptcy.

Secondly, this loan, as Mr. Geng, who is adding to the edition in this newspaper, said, "Debt is added to debt, and profit is generated from profit. The descendants and grandchildren who have not yet come out of their mother's womb will also have to accept in advance the fixed silver for working for others for free."

Also, this Sino-American loan has exposed the bloody conflicts of various imperialists in the struggle for markets. The London Times said in a report on the new Sino-American loan, "The result will increase the dissatisfaction of British creditors who hold Chinese debt." (See the 13th edition of this newspaper)

Special Document Compendium: Involuntary Voluntariness 243

(Indentured Servitude Contract) Ms. XX arrived in Shanghai only to realize that working—especially in a cotton mill or silk factory—was far worse than the life of cattle and horses in the countryside. But in this day and age, being able to get a life like cattle and horses is already fortunate. Looking back at my brothers and sisters in my hometown, they can't even get a life like cattle and horses, how painful and unfortunate it must be!

In order to get this kind of work that is worse than that of cattle and horses, my father didn't know how many good words he said to Uncle XX, and he also sent two chickens before he agreed to introduce me here. On the day I was about to leave, Uncle XX lent my father thirty yuan, and asked him to write such a contract:

"I, XX, voluntarily state that due to family difficulties this year, my daughter XX is willingly handed over to the recruiter XXX to be brought to Shanghai Cotton Mill to work. It is clearly stated in the presence of a witness that thirty silver dollars are guaranteed, with a three-year term, and this amount will be paid at ten yuan each March of each year. After entering the factory, she will be subject to the recruiter's teachings and must not disobey. If she runs away or is abducted, or if an unexpected natural disaster occurs, the signatory will be responsible, and the recruiter will not be held liable. If she has a headache or a cold, the recruiter will be responsible. During the three-year term, the recruiter will be responsible for the girl's clothing. If there is a work stoppage, compensation will be paid in full. The term expires on the XXth day of the XXth month of the XXth year. After the term expires, one month's salary shall be given to the recruiter. To prevent future disputes, this is the proof."

Looking at such a contract, then my

Page 23

current living situation can naturally be imagined! I have no freedom whatsoever. My wages, my work, and even my person, are not my own.

In order to obtain the work of cattle and horses, my father and I had no choice but to "voluntarily" write such an indenture.

Special Self-Employment Introduction

A Real Man 244

— Zi Ju

The bullets of the "January 28th Incident" shattered my rice bowl invisibly. The chain of life was broken, and I drifted like a kite without a string, without any place to land.

I am a graduate of XX County Normal School. Driven by hunger and cold, I embarked on the road of life long ago. Although I have no special skills, continuous labor has been the only typical aspect of my past life. In the past five or six years, I have worked as a clerk, teacher, copyist, and in the military.

Now I have been thrown into the vast group of unemployed. Around me are the walls formed by class, but I am still struggling, trying to break through this encirclement.

I have no home, and my father passed away long ago. In a corner of the sky, under someone else's fence, lives my white-haired, desolate mother, living a lonely and difficult life. Today, I can only wander in Shanghai, taking refuge in Uncle X's home.

Counting on my fingers, I have been unemployed for more than a year! Now it is the season of moldy rain again. I sit all day in a pigeon-cage-like room, and a square, lead-gray sky weighs heavily on my head. My brain is swelling, and I cannot freely raise my head and take a breath. I never thought that I, a twenty-four-year-old man, would have nothing to do in this blind world!

My mother is calling me back, alas! She has forgotten that I am a homeless, wandering orphan. Where should I go?

Now, if there is any copying, clerical, or other work, whether in a company, bank, school, or individual, I am willing to do it. My desire is not high, I only ask to be able to maintain my personal life. If I am employed, I will be extremely grateful! Please forward replies through this publication. I am waiting with my eyes wide open!

Amateur Coffee Shop

Trendy Literati Are Not Yet Trendy Enough 245

— Yi

Let's leave the materialist sociologists aside for the moment. Even the trendy literati who know how to cater to the trends of the times are also changing their style, deliberately depicting the lives of the working masses and speaking out for their grievances; but aren't those who are languishing and groaning under capitalist society more than just this group of hard-working laborers?

The old-fashioned shop assistants have to get up at five or six in the morning to sweep the floor and take down the shop door panels. They have to attend to customers until there are no traces of people on the street and the landlady is sleeping soundly, then they can close the door and go to sleep. Sometimes they have to put down their bowls and chopsticks seven or eight times a day to attend to customers, but the price they get for a year is, at best, only a hundred gold. However, they can only blame it on fate. Who can notice that they are also living a life of slavery, no different from prisoners who have been sentenced to life imprisonment?

In addition, there are the small clerks and shop assistants in factories and department stores. On the surface, they have long gowns, shoes, and socks, everything is complete; their operations are nothing more than writing, bookkeeping, calculating with an abacus, and issuing invoices. Compared with manual laborers, it seems to be more convenient and leisurely. But they have to wear shoes, socks, and long gowns, especially they can't wear them poorly, otherwise people will say that they are detrimental to the employer's appearance. They also need to live in houses, and they also have old mothers, wives, and children to support; but how much compensation do they get for doing monotonous work for entrepreneurs all day long? In Shanghai, the average clerk or shop assistant earns a monthly salary of no more than thirty yuan at most, and as little as seven or eight yuan. With the cost of living in Shanghai being higher than everywhere else, how can they maintain their family's life? The positions they hold can be filled by managers and factory directors, and there are countless talents who are envious of them and waiting for vacancies. After all, they are not technicians, nothing special. If they make a mistake, the factory or store can immediately tell them to pack up and go home to drink the northwest wind. They have not organized any groups, and they do not receive any assistance. Their jobs are not guaranteed at all. In short, the pain they endure is like a mute eating Coptis chinensis, and has any trendy literati written an article to speak out for them?

This publication will soon launch the "Anle Life Shanghai Special Issue." We hope that writers from all walks of life will enthusiastically contribute articles. Articles that describe a life that is completely opposite to that of the poor, such as洋房, cars, big hotels,大酒, big theaters, high-class human flesh markets, the homes of rural despots, and other decadent and extravagant lives, and that can also grasp the times and have a sense of progress from time to time, are all welcome! Compensation will be generous.

A Sociological Examination of "Getting a Free Ride" in Heart Disease Sanatoriums 247

"Getting a free ride" has become a general phenomenon in Shanghai. The facts of "getting a free ride" can be seen everywhere. Especially on streetcars, "getting a free ride" by ticket collectors seems to be their regular job. Everyone who rides a streetcar has seen them "getting a free ride" with their own eyes. And the so-called ticket collectors also think that their wages are too low and not enough to live on, and that they cannot maintain themselves without "getting a free ride." In other words, in their view, "getting a free ride" has become the only way to improve their lives. This fact is said to be immoral by people who stand on the side of the capitalists' interests, and should be strictly prohibited. Other people who sympathize with the ticket collectors say that this is legitimate and should be done, especially since they are "getting a free ride" from foreigners or capitalists. We often hear this kind of argument. But according to sociological examination, these people only see the surface of the matter, and have not deeply investigated its essence. That is to say, they do not know whether "getting a free ride" is beneficial or harmful to the entire working class.

In the current society, there is no doubt that the workers are in a position of being oppressed and exploited. They sell their labor power all day long, but they cannot even get enough to eat. On the other hand, there are capitalists who do not work but reap the benefits, sitting back and extracting the surplus value of the workers all day long, living a luxurious and extravagant life. Therefore, the inequality of mankind and the phenomenon of the poor getting poorer and the rich getting richer are rooted in this, becoming the source of all evils! But history tells us that following the deepening of this phenomenon, the awakening of the workers has been awakened. They realize that whether for their own survival or for the interests of the entire working class, there is a need for struggle, and only struggle is their way out. So the struggle is constantly active between them. However, the struggle is usually from within individual industrial sectors or special occupational organizations. For example, the past water and electricity strikes, postal strikes, and cotton mill strikes were all initiated from within a single organization. At the same time, they are still based on individual or special interests. Therefore, when they struggle, the scope is often narrow and not broad. That is because they only know that the interests of workers in the same occupation are common, and that they should unite to fight for these common interests. But the fact is before us, this kind of struggle rarely has a chance of victory, and is often taught a lesson of failure. To put it another way, the interests that are won are also very important to intensify this struggle, and to further win the final victory. However, this kind of struggle does not only focus on the interests of workers in a particular occupation, but must take into account the interests of the entire working class. It must be known that the interests of the entire working class are the real interests of each individual, and that the entire working class must be united to confront the capitalists whose interests are contrary, in order to maintain the interests that have been obtained or to fight for new interests. As for all other opportunistic methods, the workers should not adopt them.

Knowing this, the advantages and disadvantages of "getting a free ride" for the workers is not difficult to understand. Strictly speaking, "getting a free ride" has no meaning in improving life, it is just an opportunistic way to escape reality, enough to reduce the mood of struggle, blur the consciousness of struggle, shift the goal of struggle, and make them give up the task of fighting for the interests of the entire working class, and only take care of the current acquisition of such illegitimate interests. Moreover, "getting a free ride" itself is risky. Once discovered by the ticket inspector, there is a risk of being fined or fired. Even if he is lucky enough to get through it peacefully, he will only get a little "extra money". Is it worth it to devote all his energy to pay attention to it, and even recognize it as the only way to improve his life? Without taking into account the interests of the entire working class, even individual struggles cannot obtain the interests of the monarch. Then, this kind of opportunistic behavior to escape reality will certainly not be beneficial to the entire working class, but is completely harmful.

Continuation of Special Publication on Living in Impoverished Areas

The Lime Kiln, Where Corpses Are Everywhere 248

— Yi Zhong

(Shacks) Lime kilns used to be places where lime was manufactured, but now they are another manifestation of urban contradictions. It is located in the middle of towering factories on all sides. Stepping out of the walls of Robinson Road, the boundary of England and China, is the boundary of the lime kiln. There are no tiled houses here, only thatched sheds. The first impression I got when I walked into the lime kiln was a grocery store. The most goods in this store are incense candles and paper horses for superstitious purposes. From this we can know the depth of superstition in the poor team, but that is also what their lives make them. They often encounter unemployment and illness, no one comes to rescue them, and they themselves have no way to find a way out for themselves. Then naturally they have to turn to the "gods" in the dark for help.

Looking from the north of this store, I can see a large wasteland. On this wasteland are scattered new coffins and packages, many of which are wrapped in rice straw, and many of which are wrapped in broken cotton quilts or burlap bags for wrapping sugar. What they are wrapped in are all dead children. They are unfortunate to be born as children of poor families. Their parents struggle for life all day long, but they still cannot get enough to eat. Of course, these many children will not have enough to eat or wear. In times of hunger and cold, they are often locked in thatched huts exposed to wind and rain. No matter how much you cry, their parents are selling their labor far, far away for a living. Although their love for their children is no less than that of the rich, they can only sigh and express their inner pain, except for thinking about it from time to time. These many children are sick! Not only is there no money to hire a doctor to take medicine, but there is also no good care for them. Their parents can only shed some sad tears for their children, but they can only watch their beloved children get cold! Stiff! Die! There is no money to buy a coffin, so they have to wrap it in rice straw and throw it on the wasteland. In such a slum, needless to say, the child mortality rate is particularly high. Every few days, the Pushan Villa comes to the wasteland to clean up once, and each time they can receive many!

Looking west from this store again, there is a big road! A dirt road, lined with many thatched houses on both sides, the eaves of which are level with my shoulders, because this dirt road is two or three feet higher than the ground on both sides. I walked to a door and saw an old man sitting there, so I walked down the road to greet him and asked the following questions:

Question: Grandpa, how many years have you lived here?

Answer: Five or six years.

Question: Do you have to pay rent?

Answer: The rent is not paid, because we built the thatched house ourselves, but the land rent is fifteen yuan a year, and there are also thatched house donations and the rules of the big township, which also cost more than twenty yuan a year.

Question: This road is higher than the ground in the house, will water flow in when it rains?

Answer: Yes, so we build our thresholds very high. Small rains don't matter, but when it rains heavily, not only does the water flow in from the front, but it also flows down from the roof. So when it rains heavily, we can't even cook, only the sounds of crying and wailing. Also, the pigs that are raised run around outside when it's sunny, and when it rains, they burrow into the house and lie under the bed where people sleep, then it smells so bad!

Question: How many meals do you eat a day?

Answer: There is no fixed number. Sometimes we eat three meals, sometimes two meals, one meal, or everyone eats one meal of porridge a day. We just need not to starve to death.

Street Banquet 250

— Ms. Rong

(One-story houses) Near the section of Gaojia Lane in Ximen, there are several 18th-century impoverished buildings—one-story houses—standing among the tall buildings, making them even more short and humble.

The eaves are as tall as a person, and the scattered tiles are as sparse as an old man's teeth; a few wooden boards support the front door, the stone steps are sunken, and the floor is yellow mud; the inside of the house is dark, making it difficult to see the furnishings, only the smell of pickled vegetables drills straight into the noses of passers-by.

In the early morning, the husband carries two buckets of pickled vegetables to the vegetable market; the son plays games on the street, such as carrying marbles and rolling copper coins; the wife takes advantage of the morning's quietness and moves a stool and frame to the street to embroider gold thread flowers—worn by characters in Peking Opera, completely made of gold and silver thread wound into figures, flowers and plants, the roughest of embroideries.

In the afternoon, when the sun is imposing, the street is as hot and scalding as a steamer. They have no choice but to hide in the stuffy, small, and dark one-story houses.

Dusk, especially early summer dusk, is their active period. The faded table, stools of different shapes, round, square, high, low, long and short, are moved to the center of the street. The mismatched bowls and chopsticks are filled with yellow rice and vegetables without oil. They stuff their mouths with large and small bites at the table and in their hands.

The men, with one foot cocked on the stool, eat and speak, waving their hands and shaking their heads, so busy that they have no free time.

The women, fanning themselves with palm-leaf fans, gossip about the east and west families, giggling and talking loudly. The children, holding rice bowls with a small amount of vegetables on top, sit on the stone steps, exchanging "You give me a slice of vegetable," "I'll give you a radish," and eating with relish.

What a romantic and innocent street banquet! Do the gentlemen's gatherings and the refined people's picnics have such freedom and ease?

The sky gradually darkened, the street lights came on, the street banquet was over, and the conversation began!

The street is quiet, the street lights are yellow, and the people are gone. Only those low one-story houses, bathed in the yellow street lights, still stand peacefully and leisurely among the tall buildings.
